001package squidpony;
002
003import regexodus.*;
004import squidpony.squidmath.*;
005
006import java.io.Serializable;
007import java.util.*;
008
009/**
010 * A text generator for producing sentences and/or words in nonsense languages that fit a theme. This does not use an
011 * existing word list as a basis for its output, so it may or may not produce existing words occasionally, but you can
012 * safely assume it won't generate a meaningful sentence except in the absolute unlikeliest of cases.
013 * Created by Tommy Ettinger on 11/29/2015.
014 *
015 * @author Tommy Ettinger
016 */
017
018public class FakeLanguageGen implements Serializable {
019    private static final long serialVersionUID = -2396642435461186352L;
020    public final String[] openingVowels, midVowels, openingConsonants, midConsonants, closingConsonants,
021            vowelSplitters, closingSyllables;
022    public final boolean clean;
023    public final IntDoubleOrderedMap syllableFrequencies;
024    protected double totalSyllableFrequency = 0.0;
025    public final double vowelStartFrequency, vowelEndFrequency, vowelSplitFrequency, syllableEndFrequency;
026    public final Pattern[] sanityChecks;
027    public ArrayList<Modifier> modifiers;
028    public static final StatefulRNG srng = new StatefulRNG();
029    private static final OrderedMap<String, FakeLanguageGen> registry = new OrderedMap<>(64);
030    protected String summary = null;
031    private String name = "Nameless Language";
032    /**
033     * A pattern String that will match any vowel FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box, including Latin, Greek,
034     * and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex (as in {@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
035     */
036    public static final String anyVowel = "[àáâãäåæāăąǻǽaèéêëēĕėęěeìíîïĩīĭįıiòóôõöøōŏőœǿoùúûüũūŭůűųuýÿŷỳyαοειυаеёийоуъыэюя]",
037    /**
038     * A pattern String that will match one or more of any vowels FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box, including
039     * Latin, Greek, and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex (as in 
040     * {@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
041     */
042    anyVowelCluster = anyVowel + '+',
043    /**
044     * A pattern String that will match any consonant FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box, including Latin,
045     * Greek, and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex (as in
046     * {@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
047     */
048    anyConsonant = "[bcçćĉċčdþðďđfgĝğġģhĥħjĵȷkķlĺļľŀłmnñńņňŋpqrŕŗřsśŝşšștţťțvwŵẁẃẅxyýÿŷỳzźżžṛṝḷḹḍṭṅṇṣṃḥρσζτκχνθμπψβλγφξςбвгдклпрстфхцжмнзчшщ]",
049    /**
050     * A pattern String that will match one or more of any consonants FakeLanguageGen can produce out-of-the-box,
051     * including Latin, Greek, and Cyrillic; for use when a String will be interpreted as a regex (as in
052     * {@link FakeLanguageGen.Alteration}).
053     */
054    anyConsonantCluster = anyConsonant + '+';
055    protected static final Pattern repeats = Pattern.compile("(.)\\1+"),
056            vowelClusters = Pattern.compile(anyVowelCluster, REFlags.IGNORE_CASE | REFlags.UNICODE),
057            consonantClusters = Pattern.compile(anyConsonantCluster, REFlags.IGNORE_CASE | REFlags.UNICODE);
058    //latin
059    //àáâãäåæāăąǻǽaèéêëēĕėęěeìíîïĩīĭįıiòóôõöøōŏőœǿoùúûüũūŭůűųuýÿŷỳybcçćĉċčdþðďđfgĝğġģhĥħjĵȷkķlĺļľŀłmnñńņňŋpqrŕŗřsśŝşšștţťțvwŵẁẃẅxyýÿŷỳzźżžṛṝḷḹḍṭṅṇṣṃḥ
060    //ÀÁÂÃÄÅÆĀĂĄǺǼAÈÉÊËĒĔĖĘĚEÌÍÎÏĨĪĬĮIIÒÓÔÕÖØŌŎŐŒǾOÙÚÛÜŨŪŬŮŰŲUÝŸŶỲYBCÇĆĈĊČDÞÐĎĐFGĜĞĠĢHĤĦJĴȷKĶLĹĻĽĿŁMNÑŃŅŇŊPQRŔŖŘSŚŜŞŠȘTŢŤȚVWŴẀẂẄXYÝŸŶỲZŹŻŽṚṜḶḸḌṬṄṆṢṂḤ
061    //greek
062    //αοειυρσζτκχνθμπψβλγφξς
063    //ΑΟΕΙΥΡΣΖΤΚΧΝΘΜΠΨΒΛΓΦΞ
064    //cyrillic
065    //аеёийоуъыэюябвгдклпрстфхцжмнзчшщ
066    //АЕЁИЙОУЪЫЭЮЯБВГДКЛПРСТФХЦЖМНЗЧШЩ

068    static final Pattern[]
069            vulgarChecks = new Pattern[]
070            {
071                    //17 is REFlags.UNICODE | REFlags.IGNORE_CASE
072                    Pattern.compile("[sξζzkкκcсς][hнlι].{1,3}[dtтτΓг]", 17),
073                    Pattern.compile("(?:(?:[pрρ][hн])|[fd]).{1,3}[kкκcсςxхжχq]", 17), // lots of these end in a 'k' sound, huh
074                    Pattern.compile("[kкκcсςСQq][uμυνvhн]{1,3}[kкκcсςxхжχqmм]", 17),
075                    Pattern.compile("[bъыбвβЪЫБ].?[iτιyуλγУ].?[cсς]", 17),
076                    Pattern.compile("[hн][^aаαΛeезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУ][^aаαΛeезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУ]?[rяΓ]", 17),
077                    Pattern.compile("[tтτΓгcсς][iτιyуλγУ][tтτΓг]+$", 17),
078                    Pattern.compile("(?:(?:[pрρ][hн])|f)[aаαΛhн]{1,}[rяΓ][tтτΓг]", 17),
079                    Pattern.compile("[Ssξζzcсς][hн][iτιyуλγУ].?[sξζzcсς]", 17),
080                    Pattern.compile("[aаαΛ][nи][aаαΛeезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУoоюσοuμυνv]{1,2}[Ssξlιζz]", 17),
081                    Pattern.compile("[aаαΛ]([sξζz]{2})", 17),
082                    Pattern.compile("[kкκcсςСQq][hн]?[uμυνv]([hн]?)[nи]+[tтτΓг]", 17),
083                    Pattern.compile("[nиfvν]..?[jg]", 17), // might as well remove two possible slurs and a body part with one check
084                    Pattern.compile("[pрρ](?:(?:([eезξεЗΣoоюσοuμυνv])\\1)|(?:[eезξεЗΣiτιyуλγУuμυνv]+[sξζz]))", 17), // the grab bag of juvenile words
085                    Pattern.compile("[mм][hнwψшщ]?..?[rяΓ].?d", 17), // should pick up the #1 obscenity from Spanish and French
086                    Pattern.compile("[g][hн]?[aаαАΑΛeеёзξεЕЁЗΕΣ][yуλγУeеёзξεЕЁЗΕΣ]", 17), // could be inappropriate for random text
087                    Pattern.compile("[wψшщuμυνv](?:[hн]?)[aаαΛeеёзξεЗΕΣoоюσοuμυνv](?:[nи]+)[gkкκcсςxхжχq]", 17)
088            },
089            genericSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
090                    {
091                            Pattern.compile("[AEIOUaeiou]{3}"),
092                            Pattern.compile("(\\p{L})\\1\\1"),
093                            Pattern.compile("[Ii][iyqhl]"),
094                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]([aiu])\\1"),
095                            Pattern.compile("[Rr][aeiouy]+[rh]"),
096                            Pattern.compile("[Qq]u[yu]"),
097                            Pattern.compile("[^oaei]uch"),
098                            Pattern.compile("[Hh][tcszi]?h"),
099                            Pattern.compile("[Tt]t[^aeiouy]{2}"),
100                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]h([^aeiouy]|$)"),
101                            Pattern.compile("([xqy])\\1$"),
102                            Pattern.compile("[qi]y$"),
103                            Pattern.compile("[szSZrlRL]+?[^aeiouytdfgkcpbmnslrv][rlsz]"),
104                            Pattern.compile("[UIuiYy][wy]"),
105                            Pattern.compile("^[UIui][ae]"),
106                            Pattern.compile("^([^aeiouyl])\\1", 17)
107                    },
108            englishSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
109                    {
110                            Pattern.compile("[AEIOUaeiou]{3}"),
111                            Pattern.compile("(\\w)\\1\\1"),
112                            Pattern.compile("(.)\\1(.)\\2"),
113                            Pattern.compile("[Aa][ae]"),
114                            Pattern.compile("[Uu][umlkj]"),
115                            Pattern.compile("[Ii][iyqkhrl]"),
116                            Pattern.compile("[Oo][c]"),
117                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]([aiu])\\1"),
118                            Pattern.compile("[Rr][aeiouy]+[rh]"),
119                            Pattern.compile("[Qq]u[yu]"),
120                            Pattern.compile("[^oaei]uch"),
121                            Pattern.compile("[Hh][tcszi]?h"),
122                            Pattern.compile("[Tt]t[^aeiouy]{2}"),
123                            Pattern.compile("[Yy]h([^aeiouy]|$)"),
124                            Pattern.compile("[szSZrlRL]+?[^aeiouytdfgkcpbmnslr][rlsz]"),
125                            Pattern.compile("[UIuiYy][wy]"),
126                            Pattern.compile("^[UIui][ae]"),
127                            Pattern.compile("q(?:u?)$")
128                    },
129            japaneseSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
130                    {
131                            Pattern.compile("[AEIOUaeiou]{3}"),
132                            Pattern.compile("(\\w)\\1\\1"),
133                            Pattern.compile("[Tt]s[^u]"),
134                            Pattern.compile("[Ff][^u]"),
135                            Pattern.compile("[Yy][^auo]"),
136                            Pattern.compile("[Tt][ui]"),
137                            Pattern.compile("[SsZzDd]i"),
138                            Pattern.compile("[Hh]u"),
139                    },
140            arabicSanityChecks = new Pattern[]
141                    {
142                            Pattern.compile("(.)\\1\\1"),
143                            Pattern.compile("-[^aeiou](?:[^aeiou]|$)"),
144                    };

391    /*
392     * Removes accented characters from a string; if the "base" characters are non-English anyway then the result won't
393     * be an ASCII string, but otherwise it probably will be.
394     * <br>
395     * Credit to user hashable from http://stackoverflow.com/a/1215117
396     *
397     * @param str a string that may contain accented characters
398     * @return a string with all accented characters replaced with their (possibly ASCII) counterparts
399     *
400    public String removeAccents(String str) {
401        String alteredString = Normalizer.normalize(str, Normalizer.Form.NFD);
402        alteredString = diacritics.matcher(alteredString).replaceAll("");
403        alteredString = alteredString.replace('æ', 'a');
404        alteredString = alteredString.replace('œ', 'o');
405        alteredString = alteredString.replace('Æ', 'A');
406        alteredString = alteredString.replace('Œ', 'O');
407        return alteredString;
408    }*/
409
410    /**
411     * Removes accented Latin-script characters from a string; if the "base" characters are non-English anyway then the
412     * result won't be an ASCII string, but otherwise it probably will be.
413     *
414     * @param str a string that may contain accented Latin-script characters
415     * @return a string with all accented characters replaced with their (possibly ASCII) counterparts
416     */
417    public static CharSequence removeAccents(CharSequence str) {
418        CharSequence alteredString = str;
419        for (int i = 0; i < accentFinders.length; i++) {
420            alteredString = accentFinders[i].replace(alteredString);
421        }
422        return alteredString;
423    }
424
425    private FakeLanguageGen register(String languageName) {
426        summary = registry.size() + "@1";
427        registry.put(languageName,this);
428        name = languageName;
429        return copy();
430    }
431
432    private FakeLanguageGen summarize(String brief) {
433        summary = brief;
434        return this;
435    }

780    /**
781     * Swahili is one of the more commonly-spoken languages in sub-Saharan Africa, and serves mainly as a shared language
782     * that is often learned after becoming fluent in one of many other (vaguely-similar) languages of the area. An
783     * example sentence in Swahili, that this might try to imitate aesthetically, is "Mtoto mdogo amekisoma," meaning
784     * "The small child reads it" (where it is a book). A notable language feature used here is the redoubling of words,
785     * which is used in Swahili to emphasize or alter the meaning of the doubled word; here, it always repeats exactly
786     * and can't make minor changes like a real language might. This generates things like "gata-gata", "hapi-hapi", and
787     * "mimamzu-mimamzu", always separating with a hyphen here.
788     * <br>
789     * As an aside, please try to avoid the ugly stereotypes that fantasy media often assigns to speakers of African-like
790     * languages when using this or any of the generators. Many fantasy tropes come from older literature written with
791     * major cultural biases, and real-world cultural elements can be much more interesting to players than yet another
792     * depiction of a "jungle savage" with stereotypical traits. Consider drawing from existing lists of real-world
793     * technological discoveries, like https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_Africa , for
794     * inspiration when world-building; though some groups may not have developed agriculture by early medieval times,
795     * their neighbors may be working iron and studying astronomy just a short distance away.
796     * <br>
797     * Kondueyu; ma mpiyamdabota mise-mise nizakwaja alamsa amja, homa nkajupomba.
798     */
799    public static final FakeLanguageGen SWAHILI = swahili().register("Swahili");

840    /**
841     * Imitation Somali, using the Latin alphabet. Due to uncommon word structure, unusual allowed combinations of
842     * letters, and no common word roots with most familiar languages, this may seem like an unidentifiable or "alien"
843     * language to most readers. However, it's based on the Latin writing system for the Somali language (probably
844     * closest to the northern dialect), which due to the previously mentioned properties, makes it especially good for
845     * mixing with other languages to make letter combinations that seem strange to appear. It is unlikely that this
846     * particular generated language style will be familiar to readers, so it probably won't have existing stereotypes
847     * associated with the text. One early comment this received was, "it looks like a bunch of letters semi-randomly
848     * thrown together", which is probably a typical response (the comment was made by someone fluent in German and
849     * English, and most Western European languages are about as far as you can get from Somali).
850     * <br>
851     * Libor cat naqoxekh dhuugad gisiqir?
852     */
853    public static final FakeLanguageGen SOMALI = somali().register("Somali");

1210    /**
1211     * Imitation Hindi, romanized to use the Latin alphabet using accented glyphs similar to the IAST standard.
1212     * Most fonts do not support the glyphs that IAST-standard romanization of Hindi needs, so this uses alternate
1213     * glyphs from at most Latin Extended-A. Relative to the IAST standard, the glyphs {@code "ṛṝḷḹḍṭṅṇṣṃḥ"} become
1214     * {@code "ŗŕļĺđţńņşĕĭ"}, with the nth glyph in the first string being substituted with the nth glyph in the second
1215     * string. You may want to get a variant on this language with {@link #removeAccents()} if you can't display the
1216     * less-commonly-supported glyphs {@code āīūĕĭáíúóŗŕļţĺđńñņśş}. For some time SquidLib had a separate version of
1217     * imitation Hindi that was accurate to the IAST standard, but this version is more usable because font support is
1218     * much better for the glyphs it uses, so the IAST kind was removed (it added quite a bit of code for something that
1219     * was mostly unusable).
1220     * <br>
1221     * Darvāga yar; ghađhinopŕauka āĕrdur, conśaigaijo śabhodhaĕđū jiviđaudu.

1264    /**
1265     * Imitation Arabic, using mostly the Latin alphabet but with some Greek letters for tough transliteration topics.
1266     * It's hard to think of a more different (widely-spoken) language to romanize than Arabic. Written Arabic does not
1267     * ordinarily use vowels (the writing system is called an abjad, in contrast to an alphabet), and it has more than a
1268     * few sounds that are very different from those in English. This version, because of limited support in fonts and
1269     * the need for separate words to be distinguishable with regular expressions, uses somewhat-accurate digraphs or
1270     * trigraphs instead of the many accented glyphs (not necessarily supported by most fonts) in most romanizations of
1271     * Arabic, and this scheme uses no characters from outside ASCII.
1272     * <br>
1273     * Please try to be culturally-sensitive about how you use this generator. Classical Arabic (the variant that
1274     * normally marks vowels explicitly and is used to write the Qur'an) has deep religious significance in Islam, and
1275     * if you machine-generate text that (probably) isn't valid Arabic, but claim that it is real, or that it has
1276     * meaning when it actually doesn't, that would be an improper usage of what this generator is meant to do. In a
1277     * fantasy setting, you can easily confirm that the language is fictional and any overlap is coincidental; an
1278     * example of imitation Arabic in use is the Dungeons and Dragons setting, Al-Qadim, which according to one account
1279     * sounds similar to a word in real Arabic (that does not mean anything like what the designer was aiming for). In a
1280     * historical setting, FakeLanguageGen is probably "too fake" to make a viable imitation for any language, and may
1281     * just sound insulting if portrayed as realistic. You may want to mix ARABIC_ROMANIZED with a very different kind
1282     * of language, like GREEK_ROMANIZED or RUSSIAN_AUTHENTIC, to emphasize that this is not a real-world language.
1283     * <br>
1284     * Hiijakki al-aafusiib rihit, ibn-ullukh aj shwisari!
1285     */
1286    public static final FakeLanguageGen ARABIC_ROMANIZED = arabic().register("Arabic Romanized");

1408     * Somewhat close to Old Norse, which is itself very close to Icelandic, so this uses Icelandic spelling rules. Not
1409     * to be confused with the language(s) of Norway, where the Norwegian languages are called norsk, and are further
1410     * distinguished into Bokmål and Nynorsk. This should not be likely to seem like any form of Norwegian, since it
1411     * doesn't have the a-with-ring letter 'å' and has the letters eth ('Ðð') and thorn (Þþ). If you want to remove any
1412     * letters not present on a US-ASCII keyboard, you can use {@link Modifier#SIMPLIFY_NORSE} on this language or some
1413     * mix of this with other languages; it also changes some of the usage of "j" where it means the English "y" sound,
1414     * making "fjord" into "fyord", which is closer to familiar uses from East Asia like "Tokyo" and "Pyongyang".
1415     * <br>
1416     * Leyrk tjör stomri kna snó æd ðrépdápá, prygso?
1417     */
1418    public static final FakeLanguageGen NORSE = norse().register("Norse");

1480     * creature or place names in fantasy settings.

1482     * Adeni, Sainane, Caneros, Sune, Alade, Tidifi, Muni, Gito, Lixoi, Bovi...
1483     */
1484    public static final FakeLanguageGen FANTASY_NAME = GREEK_ROMANIZED.mix(
1485            RUSSIAN_ROMANIZED.mix(
1486                    FRENCH.removeAccents().mix(
1487                            JAPANESE_ROMANIZED, 0.5), 0.85), 0.925).register("Fantasy");
1488    /**
1489     * A mix of four different languages with some accented characters added onto an ASCII base, that can be good for
1490     * generating single words for creature or place names in fantasy settings that should have a "fancy" feeling from
1491     * having unnecessary accents added primarily for visual reasons.
1492     * <br>
1493     * Askieno, Blarcīnũn, Mēmida, Zizhounkô, Blęrinaf, Zemĭ, Mónazôr, Renerstă, Uskus, Toufounôr...
1494     */
1495    public static final FakeLanguageGen FANCY_FANTASY_NAME = FANTASY_NAME.addAccents(0.47, 0.07).register("Fancy Fantasy");

1656     * <br>

1658     */

1687    /**
1688     * Fantasy language that might be suitable for a language spoken by fiends, users of witchcraft, or people who seek
1689     * to emulate or worship similar groups. The tendency here is for DEMONIC to be the language used by creatures that
1690     * are considered evil because of their violence, while INFERNAL is the language used by creatures that are
1691     * considered evil because of their manipulation and deceit (DEMONIC being "chaotic evil" and INFERNAL being "lawful
1692     * evil"). The name INFERNAL refers to Dante's Inferno and the various naming conventions used for residents of Hell
1693     * in the more-modern Christian traditions (as well as some of the stylistic conventions of Old Testament figures
1694     * described as false idols, such as Moloch and Mammon). In an effort to make this distinct from the general style
1695     * of names used in ancient Hebrew (since this is specifically meant for the names of villains as opposed to normal
1696     * humans), we add in vowel splits as used in LOVECRAFT and DEMONIC, then add quite a few accented vowels. These
1697     * traits make the language especially well-suited for "deal with the Devil" written bargains, where a single accent
1698     * placed incorrectly could change the meaning of a contract and provide a way for a fiend to gain leverage.
1699     * <br>
1700     * Zézîzûth eke'iez áhìphon; úhiah îbbëphéh haîtemheû esmez...
1701     */
1702    public static final FakeLanguageGen INFERNAL = infernal().register("Infernal");

1865    /**
1866     * Imitation text from an approximation of Korean, using the Revised Romanization method that is official in South
1867     * Korea today and is easier to type. The text this makes may be hard to pronounce. Korean is interesting as a
1868     * language to imitate for a number of reasons; many of the sounds in it are rarely found elsewhere, it can cluster
1869     * consonants rather tightly (most languages don't; English does to a similar degree but Japanese hardly has any
1870     * groups of consonants), and there are many more vowel sounds without using tones (here, two or three letters are
1871     * used for a vowel, where the first can be y or w and the rest can be a, e, i, o, or u in some combination). Some
1872     * letter combinations possible here are impossible or very rare in correctly-Romanized actual Korean, such as the
1873     * rare occurrence of a single 'l' before a vowel (it normally only appears in Romanized text before a consonant or
1874     * at the end of a word).
1875     * <br>
1876     * Hyeop euryam, sonyon muk tyeok aengyankeon, koelgwaelmwak.
1877     */
1878    public static final FakeLanguageGen KOREAN_ROMANIZED = korean().register("Korean Romanized");

2050     * between consonants, though some vowel groups could be interpreted in multiple ways (such as English "maim" and
2051     * "bail", which also have regional differences in pronunciation). As the name would suggest, it strongly prefers
2052     * using the vowel "o", with it present in about half the groups, but doesn't have any preference toward or against

2055     * pronounce, but possible.

2095    /**
2096     * Fantasy/sci-fi language that could be spoken by some very-non-human culture that would typically be fitting for
2097     * an alien species. This alien language is meant to have an abrupt change mid-word for many words, with the suffix
2098     * of roughly half of words using the letter "e", which is absent from the rest of the language; these suffixes can
2099     * also use consonant clusters, which are similarly absent elsewhere. The suffixes would make sense as a historical
2100     * relic or as a linguistic holdout from a historical merger. As the name would suggest, it strongly prefers
2101     * using the vowel "u", with it present in about half the groups, and can use the umlaut accent "ü" on some vowels.
2102     * The consonants completely avoid hard sounds like "t" and "k", and don't cluster; they often have special marks.
2103     * This should be relatively easy to pronounce for an alien language, though the words are rather long.
2104     * <br>
2105     * Üweħid vuŕeħid deẃul leŋul waloyeyür; äyovavü...
2106     */
2107    public static final FakeLanguageGen ALIEN_U = alien_u().register("Alien U");

2187    /**
2188     * Fantasy language that tries to sound like the speech of a powerful and pompous dragon, using long, complex words
2189     * and a mix of hard consonants like "t" and "k", "liquid" consonants like "l" and "r", and sometimes vowel groups
2190     * like "ie" and "aa". It frequently uses consonant clusters involving "r". It uses no accented characters.
2191     * <br>
2192     * Vokegodzaaz kigrofreth ariatarkioth etrokagik deantoznik hragriemitaaz gianehaadaz...
2193     */
2194    public static final FakeLanguageGen DRAGON = dragon().register("Dragon");
2195
2196    /**
2197     * Fantasy language based closely on {@link #DRAGON}, but with much shorter words normally and closing syllables
2198     * that may sound "rushed" or "crude", though it has the same general frequency of most consonants and vowels.
2199     * This means it still uses lots of "t", "k", and "r", can group two vowels sometimes, and when there's a consonant
2200     * in the middle of a word, it is often accompanied by an "r" on one or both sides. If used with
2201     * {@link NaturalLanguageCipher}, this will look very similar to DRAGON, because the syllable lengths aren't
2202     * determined by this object but by the text being ciphered. Still, the ends of words are often different. It is
2203     * called KOBOLD because, even though the original kobold myth was that of a goblin-like spirit that haunted cobalt
2204     * mines, the modern RPG treatment of kobolds frequently describes them as worshippers of dragons or in some way
2205     * created by dragons, but generally they're a sort of failure to live up to a dragon's high expectations. The feel
2206     * of this language is meant to be something like a dragon's speech, but much less "fancy" and rather curt.
2207     * <br>
2208     * Thritriz, laazak gruz kokak thon lut...
2209     */
2210    public static final FakeLanguageGen KOBOLD = new FakeLanguageGen(
2211            DRAGON.openingVowels, DRAGON.midVowels, DRAGON.openingConsonants, DRAGON.midConsonants, DRAGON.closingConsonants,
2212            new String[]{"ik", "ak", "ek", "at", "it", "ik", "ak", "ek", "at", "it", "ik", "ak", "ek", "at", "it", "et", "ut", "ark", "irk", "erk"},
2213            DRAGON.vowelSplitters, new int[]{1, 2, 3}, new double[]{5, 11, 1},
2214            0.1, 0.0, 0.0, 0.22, genericSanityChecks, true).register("Kobold");

2418    /**
2419     * Fantasy/sci-fi language that would potentially be fitting for a trade language spoken by various very-different
2420     * groups, such as creatures with tentacled faces who need to communicate with spider-elves and living crystals.
2421     * This language tries to use relatively few sounds so vocally-restricted species can speak it or approximate it,
2422     * but some of its sounds are uncommon. It uses "ng" as Vietnamese does, as a sound that can be approximated with
2423     * "w" but more accurately is like the sound at the end of "gong". It uses a breathy sound in many vowels,
2424     * represented by "h", and this is separate from (and can be combined with) lengthening the vowel by doubling it
2425     * ("a", "ah", "aa", and "aah" are different). The "x" sound can be approximated by any of the "kh" or "q" sounds
2426     * used in various human languages, or with its usage in English for "ks". This does separate some vowels with "'",
2427     * which can be a glottal stop as in Hawaiian or various other languages, or approximated with a brief pause.
2428     * <br>
2429     * Zrolmolurz, voluu, nguu yuh'ongohng!
2430     */
2431    public static final FakeLanguageGen DEEP_SPEECH = deepSpeech().register("Deep Speech");

2433    /**
2434     * An array that stores all the hand-made FakeLanguageGen constants; it does not store randomly-generated languages
2435     * nor does it store modifications or mixes of languages. The order these are stored in is related to the numeric
2436     * codes for languages in the {@link #serializeToString()} output, but neither is dependent on the other if this
2437     * array is changed for some reason (which is not recommended, but not out of the question). If this is modified,
2438     * then it is probably a bad idea to assign null to any elements in registered; special care is taken to avoid null
2439     * elements in its original state, so some code may rely on the items being usable and non-null.
2440     */
2441    public static final FakeLanguageGen[] registered;
2442    public static final String[] registeredNames;
2443    static {
2444        // the first item in registry is null so it can be a placeholder for random languages; we want to skip it.
2445        registered = new FakeLanguageGen[registry.size()-1];
2446        registeredNames = new String[registered.length];
2447        for (int i = 0; i < registered.length; i++) {
2448            registeredNames[i] = registry.keyAt(i+1);
2449            registered[i] = registry.getAt(i+1);
2450        }
2451    }

2509    /**
2510     * This is a very complicated constructor! Maybe look at the calls to this to initialize static members of this
2511     * class, LOVECRAFT and GREEK_ROMANIZED.
2512     *
2513     * @param openingVowels        String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear at the start
2514     *                             of a word or in the middle; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2515     * @param midVowels            String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear in the
2516     *                             middle of the word; all openingVowels are automatically copied into this internally.
2517     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2518     * @param openingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster that can appear
2519     *                             at the start of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2520     * @param midConsonants        String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2521     *                             between vowels; all closingConsonants are automatically copied into this internally.
2522     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2523     * @param closingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2524     *                             at the end of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2525     * @param closingSyllables     String array where each element is a syllable starting with a vowel and ending in
2526     *                             whatever the word should end in; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2527     * @param vowelSplitters       String array where each element is a mark that goes between vowels, so if "-" is in this,
2528     *                             then "a-a" may be possible; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2529     * @param syllableLengths      int array where each element is a possible number of syllables a word can use; closely
2530     *                             tied to syllableFrequencies
2531     * @param syllableFrequencies  double array where each element corresponds to an element in syllableLengths and
2532     *                             represents how often each syllable count should appear relative to other counts; there
2533     *                             is no need to restrict the numbers to add up to any other number
2534     * @param vowelStartFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words start with vowels;
2535     *                             higher numbers yield more words starting with vowels
2536     * @param vowelEndFrequency    a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words end with vowels; higher
2537     *                             numbers yield more words ending in vowels
2538     * @param vowelSplitFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that, if vowelSplitters is not empty, determines how
2539     *                             often a vowel will be split into two vowels separated by one of those splitters
2540     * @param syllableEndFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often an element of
2541     *                             closingSyllables is used instead of ending normally
2542     */
2543    public FakeLanguageGen(String[] openingVowels, String[] midVowels, String[] openingConsonants,
2544                           String[] midConsonants, String[] closingConsonants, String[] closingSyllables, String[] vowelSplitters,
2545                           int[] syllableLengths, double[] syllableFrequencies, double vowelStartFrequency,
2546                           double vowelEndFrequency, double vowelSplitFrequency, double syllableEndFrequency) {
2547        this(openingVowels, midVowels, openingConsonants, midConsonants, closingConsonants, closingSyllables,
2548                vowelSplitters, syllableLengths, syllableFrequencies, vowelStartFrequency, vowelEndFrequency,
2549                vowelSplitFrequency, syllableEndFrequency, englishSanityChecks, true);
2550    }

2552    /**
2553     * This is a very complicated constructor! Maybe look at the calls to this to initialize static members of this
2554     * class, LOVECRAFT and GREEK_ROMANIZED.
2555     *
2556     * @param openingVowels        String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear at the start
2557     *                             of a word or in the middle; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2558     * @param midVowels            String array where each element is a vowel or group of vowels that may appear in the
2559     *                             middle of the word; all openingVowels are automatically copied into this internally.
2560     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2561     * @param openingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster that can appear
2562     *                             at the start of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2563     * @param midConsonants        String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2564     *                             between vowels; all closingConsonants are automatically copied into this internally.
2565     *                             Elements may be repeated to make them more common
2566     * @param closingConsonants    String array where each element is a consonant or consonant cluster than can appear
2567     *                             at the end of a word; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2568     * @param closingSyllables     String array where each element is a syllable starting with a vowel and ending in
2569     *                             whatever the word should end in; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2570     * @param vowelSplitters       String array where each element is a mark that goes between vowels, so if "-" is in this,
2571     *                             then "a-a" may be possible; elements may be repeated to make them more common
2572     * @param syllableLengths      int array where each element is a possible number of syllables a word can use; closely
2573     *                             tied to syllableFrequencies
2574     * @param syllableFrequencies  double array where each element corresponds to an element in syllableLengths and
2575     *                             represents how often each syllable count should appear relative to other counts; there
2576     *                             is no need to restrict the numbers to add up to any other number
2577     * @param vowelStartFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words start with vowels;
2578     *                             higher numbers yield more words starting with vowels
2579     * @param vowelEndFrequency    a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often words end with vowels; higher
2580     *                             numbers yield more words ending in vowels
2581     * @param vowelSplitFrequency  a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that, if vowelSplitters is not empty, determines how
2582     *                             often a vowel will be split into two vowels separated by one of those splitters
2583     * @param syllableEndFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often an element of
2584     *                             closingSyllables is used instead of ending normally
2585     * @param sane                 true to perform sanity checks for pronounce-able sounds to most English speakers, replacing many
2586     *                             words that are impossible to say; slows down generation slightly, irrelevant for non-Latin alphabets
2587     * @param clean                true to perform vulgarity/obscenity checks on the word, replacing it if it is too close to a
2588     *                             common English vulgarity, obscenity, or slur/epithet; slows down generation slightly
2589     */
2590    public FakeLanguageGen(String[] openingVowels, String[] midVowels, String[] openingConsonants,
2591                           String[] midConsonants, String[] closingConsonants, String[] closingSyllables, String[] vowelSplitters,
2592                           int[] syllableLengths, double[] syllableFrequencies, double vowelStartFrequency,
2593                           double vowelEndFrequency, double vowelSplitFrequency, double syllableEndFrequency,
2594                           Pattern[] sane, boolean clean) {
2595        this.openingVowels = openingVowels;
2596        this.midVowels = new String[openingVowels.length + midVowels.length];
2597        System.arraycopy(midVowels, 0, this.midVowels, 0, midVowels.length);
2598        System.arraycopy(openingVowels, 0, this.midVowels, midVowels.length, openingVowels.length);
2599        this.openingConsonants = openingConsonants;
2600        this.midConsonants = new String[midConsonants.length + closingConsonants.length];
2601        System.arraycopy(midConsonants, 0, this.midConsonants, 0, midConsonants.length);
2602        System.arraycopy(closingConsonants, 0, this.midConsonants, midConsonants.length, closingConsonants.length);
2603        this.closingConsonants = closingConsonants;
2604        this.vowelSplitters = vowelSplitters;
2605        this.closingSyllables = closingSyllables;
2606
2607        this.syllableFrequencies = new IntDoubleOrderedMap(syllableLengths, syllableFrequencies, 0.75f);
2608
2609        totalSyllableFrequency = this.syllableFrequencies.values().sum();
2610        if (vowelStartFrequency > 1.0)
2611            this.vowelStartFrequency = 1.0 / vowelStartFrequency;
2612        else
2613            this.vowelStartFrequency = vowelStartFrequency;
2614        if (vowelEndFrequency > 1.0)
2615            this.vowelEndFrequency = 1.0 / vowelEndFrequency;
2616        else
2617            this.vowelEndFrequency = vowelEndFrequency;
2618        if (vowelSplitters.length == 0)
2619            this.vowelSplitFrequency = 0.0;
2620        else if (vowelSplitFrequency > 1.0)
2621            this.vowelSplitFrequency = 1.0 / vowelSplitFrequency;
2622        else
2623            this.vowelSplitFrequency = vowelSplitFrequency;
2624        if (closingSyllables.length == 0)
2625            this.syllableEndFrequency = 0.0;
2626        else if (syllableEndFrequency > 1.0)
2627            this.syllableEndFrequency = 1.0 / syllableEndFrequency;
2628        else
2629            this.syllableEndFrequency = syllableEndFrequency;
2630        this.clean = clean;
2631        sanityChecks = sane;
2632        modifiers = new ArrayList<>(16);
2633    }
2634
2635    private FakeLanguageGen(String[] openingVowels, String[] midVowels, String[] openingConsonants,
2636                            String[] midConsonants, String[] closingConsonants, String[] closingSyllables,
2637                            String[] vowelSplitters, IntDoubleOrderedMap syllableFrequencies,
2638                            double vowelStartFrequency, double vowelEndFrequency, double vowelSplitFrequency,
2639                            double syllableEndFrequency, Pattern[] sanityChecks, boolean clean,
2640                            List<Modifier> modifiers) {
2641        this.openingVowels = copyStrings(openingVowels);
2642        this.midVowels = copyStrings(midVowels);
2643        this.openingConsonants = copyStrings(openingConsonants);
2644        this.midConsonants = copyStrings(midConsonants);
2645        this.closingConsonants = copyStrings(closingConsonants);
2646        this.closingSyllables = copyStrings(closingSyllables);
2647        this.vowelSplitters = copyStrings(vowelSplitters);
2648        this.syllableFrequencies = new IntDoubleOrderedMap(syllableFrequencies);
2649        this.vowelStartFrequency = vowelStartFrequency;
2650        this.vowelEndFrequency = vowelEndFrequency;
2651        this.vowelSplitFrequency = vowelSplitFrequency;
2652        this.syllableEndFrequency = syllableEndFrequency;
2653        for (Double freq : this.syllableFrequencies.values()) {
2654            totalSyllableFrequency += freq;
2655        }
2656        if (sanityChecks == null)
2657            this.sanityChecks = null;
2658        else {
2659            this.sanityChecks = new Pattern[sanityChecks.length];
2660            System.arraycopy(sanityChecks, 0, this.sanityChecks, 0, sanityChecks.length);
2661        }
2662        this.clean = clean;
2663        this.modifiers = new ArrayList<>(modifiers);
2664    }
2665
2666    private static String[] processParts(OrderedMap<String, String> parts, Set<String> missingSounds,
2667                                         Set<String> forbidden, IRNG rng, double repeatSingleChance,
2668                                         int preferredLimit) {
2669        int l, sz = parts.size();
2670        List<String> working = new ArrayList<>(sz * 24);
2671        String pair;
2672        for (int e = 0; e < parts.size(); e++) {
2673            Map.Entry<String, String> sn = parts.entryAt(e);
2674            if (missingSounds.contains(sn.getKey()))
2675                continue;
2676            for (String t : sn.getValue().split(" ")) {
2677                if (forbidden.contains(t))
2678                    continue;
2679                l = t.length();
2680                int num;
2681                char c;
2682                switch (l) {
2683                    case 0:
2684                        break;
2685                    case 1:
2686                        working.add(t);
2687                        working.add(t);
2688                        working.add(t);
2689                        c = t.charAt(0);
2690                        num = 0;
2691                        boolean repeat = true;
2692                        switch (c) {
2693                            case 'w':
2694                                num += 2;
2695                            case 'y':
2696                            case 'h':
2697                                num += 4;
2698                            case 'q':
2699                            case 'x':
2700                                num += 4;
2701                                repeat = false;
2702                                break;
2703                            case 'i':
2704                            case 'u':
2705                                repeat = false;
2706                                num = 13;
2707                                break;
2708                            case 'z':
2709                            case 'v':
2710                                num = 4;
2711                                break;
2712                            case 'j':
2713                                num = 7;
2714                                break;
2715                            default:
2716                                if (e >= preferredLimit)
2717                                    num = 6;
2718                                else
2719                                    num = 13;
2720                        }
2721                        for (int i = 0; i < num * 3; i++) {
2722                            if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.75) {
2723                                working.add(t);
2724                            }
2725                        }
2726
2727                        if (repeat && rng.nextDouble() < repeatSingleChance) {
2728                            pair = t + t;
2729                            if (missingSounds.contains(pair))
2730                                continue;
2731                            working.add(pair);
2732                            working.add(pair);
2733                            working.add(pair);
2734                            if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.7) {
2735                                working.add(pair);
2736                                working.add(pair);
2737                            }
2738                            if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.7) {
2739                                working.add(pair);
2740                            }
2741                        }
2742
2743                        break;
2744                    case 2:
2745                        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.65) {
2746                            c = t.charAt(1);
2747                            num = 0;
2748                            switch (c) {
2749                                case 'z':
2750                                    num = 1;
2751                                    break;
2752                                case 'w':
2753                                    num = 3;
2754                                    break;
2755                                case 'n':
2756                                    num = 4;
2757                                    break;
2758                                default:
2759
2760                                    if (e >= preferredLimit)
2761                                        num = 2;
2762                                    else
2763                                        num = 7;
2764                            }
2765                            working.add(t);
2766                            for (int i = 0; i < num; i++) {
2767                                if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.25) {
2768                                    working.add(t);
2769                                }
2770                            }
2771                        }
2772                        break;
2773                    case 3:
2774                        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.5) {
2775                            c = t.charAt(0);
2776                            switch (c) {
2777                                case 'z':
2778                                    num = 1;
2779                                    break;
2780                                case 'w':
2781                                    num = 3;
2782                                    break;
2783                                case 'n':
2784                                    num = 4;
2785                                    break;
2786                                default:
2787                                    if (e >= preferredLimit)
2788                                        num = 2;
2789                                    else
2790                                        num = 6;
2791                            }
2792                            working.add(t);
2793                            for (int i = 0; i < num; i++) {
2794                                if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.2) {
2795                                    working.add(t);
2796                                }
2797                            }
2798                        }
2799                        break;
2800                    default:
2801                        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.3 && (t.charAt(l - 1) != 'z' || rng.nextDouble() < 0.1)) {
2802                            working.add(t);
2803                        }
2804                        break;
2805                }
2806            }
2807        }
2808        return working.toArray(new String[0]);
2809    }

2824    public static FakeLanguageGen randomLanguage(long seed) {
2825        StatefulRNG rng = new StatefulRNG(seed);
2826        int[] lengths = new int[rng.between(3, 5)];
2827        System.arraycopy(new int[]{1, 2, 3, 4}, 0, lengths, 0, lengths.length);
2828        double[] chances = new double[lengths.length];
2829        System.arraycopy(new double[]{
2830                5 + rng.nextDouble(4), 13 + rng.nextDouble(9), 3 + rng.nextDouble(3), 1 + rng.nextDouble(2)
2831        }, 0, chances, 0, chances.length);
2832        double vowelHeavy = rng.between(0.2, 0.5), removalRate = rng.between(0.15, 0.65);
2833        int sz = openCons.size();
2834        int[] reordering = rng.randomOrdering(sz), vOrd = rng.randomOrdering(openVowels.size());
2835        OrderedMap<String, String>
2836                parts0 = new OrderedMap<>(openVowels),
2837                parts1 = new OrderedMap<>(openCons),
2838                parts2 = new OrderedMap<>(midCons),
2839                parts3 = new OrderedMap<>(closeCons);
2840        OrderedSet<String> forbidden = new OrderedSet<>(1024, 0.25f), missingSounds = new OrderedSet<>(64, 0.875f);
2841        parts1.reorder(reordering);
2842        parts2.reorder(reordering);
2843        parts3.reorder(reordering);
2844        parts0.reorder(vOrd);
2845        int n = 0;
2846
2847        int mn = Math.min(rng.nextInt(3), rng.nextInt(3)), sz0, p0s;
2848
2849        for (n = 0; n < mn; n++) {
2850            missingSounds.add(parts0.keyAt(0));
2851            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts0.getAt(0).split(" "));
2852            parts0.removeFirst();
2853        }
2854        p0s = parts0.size();
2855        sz0 = Math.max(rng.between(1, p0s + 1), rng.between(1, p0s + 1));
2856        char[] nextAccents = new char[sz0], unaccented = new char[sz0];
2857        int vowelAccent = rng.between(1, 7);
2858        for (int i = 0; i < sz0; i++) {
2859            nextAccents[i] = accentedVowels[vOrd[i + mn]][vowelAccent];
2860            unaccented[i] = accentedVowels[vOrd[i + mn]][0];
2861        }
2862        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.8) {
2863            for (int i = 0; i < sz0; i++) {
2864                char ac = nextAccents[i], ua = unaccented[i];
2865                String v = "", uas = String.valueOf(ua);
2866                Pattern pat = Pattern.compile("\\b([aeiou]*)(" + ua + ")([aeiou]*)\\b");
2867                Replacer rep = pat.replacer("$1$2$3 $1" + ac + "$3"), repLess = pat.replacer("$1" + ac + "$3");
2868                for (int j = 0; j < p0s; j++) {
2869                    String k = parts0.keyAt(j);
2870                    if (uas.equals(k)) // uas is never null, always length 1
2871                        v = parts0.getAt(j);
2872                    else {
2873                        String current = parts0.getAt(j);
2874                        String[] splits = current.split(" ");
2875                        for (int s = 0; s < splits.length; s++) {
2876                            if (forbidden.contains(uas) && splits[s].contains(uas))
2877                                forbidden.add(splits[s].replace(ua, ac));
2878                        }
2879                        parts0.put(k, rep.replace(current));
2880                    }
2881                }
2882                parts0.put(String.valueOf(ac), repLess.replace(v));
2883            }
2884        }
2885
2886        n = 0;
2887        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.75) {
2888            missingSounds.add("z");
2889            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("z").split(" "));
2890            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("z").split(" "));
2891            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("z").split(" "));
2892            n++;
2893        }
2894        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.82) {
2895            missingSounds.add("x");
2896            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("x").split(" "));
2897            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("x").split(" "));
2898            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("x").split(" "));
2899            n++;
2900        }
2901        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.92) {
2902            missingSounds.add("qu");
2903            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("qu").split(" "));
2904            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("qu").split(" "));
2905            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("qu").split(" "));
2906            n++;
2907        }
2908        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.96) {
2909            missingSounds.add("q");
2910            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("q").split(" "));
2911            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("q").split(" "));
2912            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("q").split(" "));
2913            n++;
2914        }
2915        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.97) {
2916            missingSounds.add("tl");
2917            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("tl").split(" "));
2918            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("tl").split(" "));
2919            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("tl").split(" "));
2920            n++;
2921        }
2922        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.86) {
2923            missingSounds.add("ph");
2924            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("ph").split(" "));
2925            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("ph").split(" "));
2926            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("ph").split(" "));
2927            n++;
2928        }
2929        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.94) {
2930            missingSounds.add("kh");
2931            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("kh").split(" "));
2932            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("kh").split(" "));
2933            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("kh").split(" "));
2934            n++;
2935        }
2936        if (rng.nextDouble() < 0.96) {
2937            missingSounds.add("bh");
2938            missingSounds.add("dh");
2939            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("bh").split(" "));
2940            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("bh").split(" "));
2941            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("bh").split(" "));
2942            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.get("dh").split(" "));
2943            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.get("dh").split(" "));
2944            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.get("dh").split(" "));
2945            n++;
2946            n++;
2947        }
2948
2949        for (; n < sz * removalRate; n++) {
2950            missingSounds.add(parts1.keyAt(n));
2951            missingSounds.add(parts2.keyAt(n));
2952            missingSounds.add(parts3.keyAt(n));
2953            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts1.getAt(n).split(" "));
2954            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts2.getAt(n).split(" "));
2955            Collections.addAll(forbidden, parts3.getAt(n).split(" "));
2956        }
2957
2958        return new FakeLanguageGen(
2959                processParts(parts0, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, 0.0, p0s),
2960                new String[]{},
2961                processParts(openCons, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, 0.0, 4096),
2962                processParts(midCons, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, (rng.nextDouble() * 3 - 0.75) * 0.4444, 4096),
2963                processParts(closeCons, missingSounds, forbidden, rng, (rng.nextDouble() * 3 - 0.75) * 0.2857, 4096),
2964                new String[]{},
2965                new String[]{}, lengths, chances, vowelHeavy, vowelHeavy * 1.8, 0.0, 0.0, genericSanityChecks, true).summarize("0#" + seed + "@1");
2966    }

2968    protected static boolean checkAll(CharSequence testing, Pattern[] checks) {
2969        CharSequence fixed = removeAccents(testing);
2970        for (int i = 0; i < checks.length; i++) {
2971            if (checks[i].matcher(fixed).find())
2972                return false;
2973        }
2974        return true;
2975    }

2977    /**
2978     * Checks a CharSequence, such as a String, against an overzealous vulgarity filter, returning true if the text
2979     * could contain vulgar elements or words that could seem vulgar or juvenile. The idea here is that false positives
2980     * are OK as long as there are very few false negatives (missed vulgar words). Does not check punctuation or numbers
2981     * that could look like letters.
2982     * @param testing the text, as a CharSequence such as a String, to check
2983     * @return true if the text could contain a vulgar or juvenile element; false if it probably doesn't
2984     */
2985    public static boolean checkVulgarity(CharSequence testing)
2986    {
2987        CharSequence fixed = removeAccents(testing);
2988        for (int i = 0; i < vulgarChecks.length; i++) {
2989            if (vulgarChecks[i].matcher(fixed).find())
2990            {
2991                System.out.println(vulgarChecks[i]);
2992                return true;
2993            }
2994        }
2995        return false;
2996    }

3021    /**
3022     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen using the specified RNG.
3023     *
3024     * @param rng        the RNG to use for the randomized string building
3025     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
3026     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
3027     */
3028    public String word(IRNG rng, boolean capitalize) {
3029        while (true) {
3030            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(20), ender = new StringBuilder(12);
3031            double syllableChance = rng.nextDouble(totalSyllableFrequency);
3032            int syllables = 1, i = 0;
3033            for (IntDoubleOrderedMap.MapEntry kv : syllableFrequencies.mapEntrySet()) {
3034                if (syllableChance < kv.getDoubleValue()) {
3035                    syllables = kv.getIntKey();
3036                    break;
3037                } else
3038                    syllableChance -= kv.getDoubleValue();
3039            }
3040            if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelStartFrequency) {
3041                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
3042                if (syllables == 1)
3043                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3044                else
3045                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3046                i++;
3047            } else {
3048                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingConsonants));
3049            }
3050            String close = "";
3051            boolean redouble = false;
3052            if (i < syllables) {
3053                if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3054                    close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3055                    if (close.contains("@") && (syllables & 1) == 0) {
3056                        redouble = true;
3057                        syllables = (syllables | 1) >> 1;
3058
3059                        //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
3060                    }
3061                    if (!close.contains("@"))
3062                        ender.append(close);
3063                    else if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelEndFrequency) {
3064                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3065                        if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3066                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3067                                    .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3068                        }
3069                    }
3070                } else {
3071                    ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3072                    if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3073                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3074                                .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3075                    }
3076                    if (rng.nextDouble() >= vowelEndFrequency) {
3077                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3078                        if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3079                            close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3080                            if (close.contains("@") && (syllables & 1) == 0) {
3081                                redouble = true;
3082                                syllables = (syllables | 1) >> 1;
3083
3084                                //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
3085                            }
3086                            if (!close.contains("@"))
3087                                ender.append(close);
3088                        }
3089                    }
3090                }
3091                i += vowelClusters.matcher(ender).findAll().count();
3092
3093            }
3094
3095            for (; i < syllables; i++) {
3096                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3097                if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3098                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3099                            .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3100                }
3101                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3102            }
3103
3104            sb.append(ender);
3105            if (redouble && i <= syllables + 1) {
3106                sb.append(close.replaceAll("@", sb.toString()));
3107            }
3108
3109            if (sanityChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, sanityChecks))
3110                continue;
3111
3112            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
3113                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
3114            }
3115
3116            if (capitalize)
3117                sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
3118
3119            if (clean && !checkAll(sb, vulgarChecks))
3120                continue;
3121            return sb.toString();
3122        }
3123    }

3165    public String word(long seed, boolean capitalize, int approxSyllables, Pattern[] additionalChecks) {

3170    /**
3171     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen using the specified RNG with an approximate number of syllables.
3172     * This takes an array of {@link Pattern} objects (from RegExodus, not java.util.regex) that should match invalid
3173     * outputs, such as words that shouldn't be generated in some context due to vulgarity or cultural matters.
3174     *
3175     * @param rng        the RNG to use for the randomized string building
3176     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
3177     * @param approxSyllables the approximate number of syllables to produce in the word; there may be more syllables
3178     * @param additionalChecks an array of RegExodus Pattern objects that match invalid words (these may be additional vulgarity checks, for example)
3179     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
3180     */
3181    public String word(IRNG rng, boolean capitalize, int approxSyllables, Pattern[] additionalChecks) {
3182        if (approxSyllables <= 0) {
3183            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
3184            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
3185                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
3186            }
3187            if (capitalize) sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
3188            return sb.toString();
3189        }
3190        while (true) {
3191            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(20), ender = new StringBuilder(12);
3192            int i = 0;
3193            if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelStartFrequency) {
3194                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
3195                if (approxSyllables == 1 && closingConsonants.length > 0)
3196                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3197                else if (midConsonants.length > 0)
3198                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3199                i++;
3200            } else if (openingConsonants.length > 0) {
3201                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingConsonants));
3202            }
3203            String close = "";
3204            boolean redouble = false;
3205            if (i < approxSyllables) {
3206                if (closingSyllables.length > 0 && rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3207                    close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3208                    if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
3209                        redouble = true;
3210                        approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
3211
3212                        //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
3213                    }
3214                    if (!close.contains("@"))
3215                        ender.append(close);
3216                    else if (redouble && rng.nextDouble() < vowelEndFrequency) {
3217                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3218                        if (vowelSplitters.length > 0 && rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3219                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3220                                    .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3221                        }
3222                    }
3223                } else {
3224                    ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3225                    if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3226                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3227                                .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3228                    }
3229                    if (rng.nextDouble() >= vowelEndFrequency) {
3230                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3231                        if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3232                            close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3233                            if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
3234                                redouble = true;
3235                                approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
3236
3237                                //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
3238                            }
3239                            if (!close.contains("@"))
3240                                ender.append(close);
3241                        }
3242                    }
3243                }
3244                i += vowelClusters.matcher(ender).findAll().count();
3245            }
3246
3247            for (; i < approxSyllables; i++) {
3248                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3249                if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3250                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3251                            .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3252                }
3253                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3254            }
3255
3256            sb.append(ender);
3257            if (redouble && i <= approxSyllables + 1) {
3258                sb.append(close.replaceAll("@", sb.toString()));
3259            }
3260
3261            if (sanityChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, sanityChecks))
3262                continue;
3263
3264            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
3265                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
3266            }
3267
3268            if (clean && !checkAll(sb, vulgarChecks))
3269                continue;
3270
3271            if (additionalChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, additionalChecks))
3272                continue;
3273
3274            if (capitalize)
3275                sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
3276
3277            return sb.toString();
3278        }
3279    }
3280
3281    /**
3282     * Generate a word from this FakeLanguageGen using the specified StatefulRNG with an approximate number of
3283     * syllables, potentially setting the state of rng mid-way through the word to another seed from {@code reseeds}
3284     * more than once if the word is long enough. This overload is less likely to be used very often.
3285     *
3286     * @param rng        the StatefulRNG to use for the randomized string building
3287     * @param capitalize true if the word should start with a capital letter, false otherwise
3288     * @param approxSyllables the approximate number of syllables to produce in the word; there may be more syllables
3289     * @param reseeds an array or varargs of additional long seeds to seed {@code rng} with mid-generation 
3290     * @return a word in the fake language as a String
3291     */
3292    public String word(StatefulRNG rng, boolean capitalize, int approxSyllables, long... reseeds) {
3293        if (approxSyllables <= 0) {
3294            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
3295            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
3296                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
3297            }
3298            if (capitalize) sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
3299            return sb.toString();
3300        }
3301        int numSeeds, fraction = 1;
3302        if (reseeds != null)
3303            numSeeds = Math.min(reseeds.length, approxSyllables - 1);
3304        else numSeeds = 0;
3305        while (true) {
3306            StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(20), ender = new StringBuilder(12);
3307            int i = 0;
3308            if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelStartFrequency) {
3309                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingVowels));
3310                if (approxSyllables == 1)
3311                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3312                else
3313                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3314                i++;
3315            } else {
3316                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(openingConsonants));
3317            }
3318            String close = "";
3319            boolean redouble = false;
3320            if (i < approxSyllables) {
3321                if (numSeeds > 0 && i > 0 && i == approxSyllables * fraction / (1 + numSeeds))
3322                    rng.setState(reseeds[fraction++ - 1]);
3323                if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3324                    close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3325                    if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
3326                        redouble = true;
3327                        approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
3328                    }
3329                    if (!close.contains("@"))
3330                        ender.append(close);
3331                    else if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelEndFrequency) {
3332                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3333                        if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3334                            ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3335                                    .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3336                        }
3337                    }
3338                } else {
3339                    ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3340                    if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3341                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3342                                .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3343                    }
3344                    if (rng.nextDouble() >= vowelEndFrequency) {
3345                        ender.append(rng.getRandomElement(closingConsonants));
3346                        if (rng.nextDouble() < syllableEndFrequency) {
3347                            close = rng.getRandomElement(closingSyllables);
3348                            if (close.contains("@") && (approxSyllables & 1) == 0) {
3349                                redouble = true;
3350                                approxSyllables = approxSyllables >> 1;
3351
3352                                //sb.append(close.replaceAll("@\\d", sb.toString()));
3353                            }
3354                            if (!close.contains("@"))
3355                                ender.append(close);
3356                        }
3357                    }
3358                }
3359                i += vowelClusters.matcher(ender).findAll().count();
3360            }
3361
3362            for (; i < approxSyllables; i++) {
3363                if (numSeeds > 0 && i > 0 && i == approxSyllables * fraction / (1 + numSeeds))
3364                    rng.setState(reseeds[fraction++ - 1]);
3365                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3366                if (rng.nextDouble() < vowelSplitFrequency) {
3367                    sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(vowelSplitters))
3368                            .append(rng.getRandomElement(midVowels));
3369                }
3370                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midConsonants));
3371            }
3372
3373            sb.append(ender);
3374            if (redouble && i <= approxSyllables + 1) {
3375                sb.append(close.replaceAll("@", sb.toString()));
3376            }
3377
3378            if (sanityChecks != null && !checkAll(sb, sanityChecks))
3379                continue;
3380
3381            for (Modifier mod : modifiers) {
3382                sb = mod.modify(rng, sb);
3383            }
3384
3385            if (capitalize)
3386                sb.setCharAt(0, Character.toUpperCase(sb.charAt(0)));
3387
3388            if (clean && !checkAll(sb, vulgarChecks))
3389                continue;
3390            return sb.toString();
3391        }
3392    }

3482    /**
3483     * Generate a sentence from this FakeLanguageGen using the specific RNG. The sentence's length in
3484     * words will be between minWords and maxWords, both inclusive. It will put one of the punctuation Strings from
3485     * {@code midPunctuation} between two words (before the space) at a frequency of {@code midPunctuationFrequency}
3486     * (between 0 and 1), and will end the sentence with one String chosen from {@code endPunctuation}.
3487     *
3488     * @param rng                     the RNG to use for the randomized string building
3489     * @param minWords                an int for the minimum number of words in a sentence; should be at least 1
3490     * @param maxWords                an int for the maximum number of words in a sentence; should be at least equal to minWords
3491     * @param midPunctuation          a String array where each element is a comma, semicolon, or the like that goes before a
3492     *                                space in the middle of a sentence
3493     * @param endPunctuation          a String array where each element is a period, question mark, or the like that goes at
3494     *                                the very end of a sentence
3495     * @param midPunctuationFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often Strings from
3496     *                                midPunctuation should be inserted before spaces
3497     * @return a sentence in the fake language as a String
3498     */
3499    public String sentence(IRNG rng, int minWords, int maxWords, String[] midPunctuation, String[] endPunctuation,
3500                           double midPunctuationFrequency) {
3501        if (minWords < 1)
3502            minWords = 1;
3503        if (minWords > maxWords)
3504            maxWords = minWords;
3505        if (midPunctuationFrequency > 1.0) {
3506            midPunctuationFrequency = 1.0 / midPunctuationFrequency;
3507        }
3508        StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder(12 * maxWords);
3509        sb.append(word(rng, true));
3510        for (int i = 1; i < minWords; i++) {
3511            if (rng.nextDouble() < midPunctuationFrequency) {
3512                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midPunctuation));
3513            }
3514            sb.append(' ').append(word(rng, false));
3515        }
3516        for (int i = minWords; i < maxWords && rng.nextInt(2 * maxWords) > i; i++) {
3517            if (rng.nextDouble() < midPunctuationFrequency) {
3518                sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(midPunctuation));
3519            }
3520            sb.append(' ').append(word(rng, false));
3521        }
3522        if (endPunctuation != null && endPunctuation.length > 0)
3523            sb.append(rng.getRandomElement(endPunctuation));
3524        return sb.toString();
3525    }

3529     * words will be between minWords and maxWords, both inclusive, unless it would exceed maxChars, in which case it is
3530     * truncated. It will put one of the punctuation Strings from {@code midPunctuation} between two words (before the
3531     * space) at a frequency of {@code midPunctuationFrequency} (between 0 and 1), and will end the sentence with one
3532     * String chosen from {@code endPunctuation}.
3533     *
3534     * @param minWords                an int for the minimum number of words in a sentence; should be at least 1
3535     * @param maxWords                an int for the maximum number of words in a sentence; should be at least equal to minWords
3536     * @param midPunctuation          a String array where each element is a comma, semicolon, or the like that goes before a
3537     *                                space in the middle of a sentence
3538     * @param endPunctuation          a String array where each element is a period, question mark, or the like that goes at
3539     *                                the very end of a sentence
3540     * @param midPunctuationFrequency a double between 0.0 and 1.0 that determines how often Strings from
3541     *                                midPunctuation should be inserted before spaces
3542     * @param maxChars                the longest string length this can produce; should be at least {@code 6 * minWords}
3543     * @return a sentence in the fake language as a String
3544     */
3545    public String sentence(int minWords, int maxWords, String[] midPunctuation, String[] endPunctuation,
3546                           double midPunctuationFrequency, int maxChars) {
